# End-to-End: How Kubernetes Creates a Deployment

## Your Task

You are onboarding to the Kubernetes project. A senior engineer has asked you to produce
a technical explanation of how a Kubernetes Deployment gets created — tracing the full
request flow from a client application through the API server and into persistent storage.

**Your question**: Explain how a Kubernetes client application creates a Deployment from
start to finish. Your explanation must trace through all three layers:

1. **Client library** — What type/function in `kubernetes-client-go` sends the HTTP request?
2. **API server** — What function in `kubernetes/kubernetes` receives and validates the create request?
3. **Storage** — What function in `etcd-io/etcd` persists the Deployment to the key-value store?

For each step, cite the specific repository, file path, and function/type name.

## Context

You are working in a Kubernetes ecosystem with the following repos:

- `kubernetes/kubernetes` (the core orchestrator)
- `sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go` (go-client-library)
- `sg-evals/kubernetes-api` (api-type-definitions)
- `etcd-io/etcd` (distributed-kv-store)

This question is specifically designed to benefit from cross-repo synthesis. Use your
search tools to trace the full path across repositories.

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings:

```json
{
  "chain": [
    {
      "repo": "sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go",
      "path": "relative/path/to/file.go",
      "symbol": "FunctionOrTypeName",
      "description": "What this step does in the flow"
    }
  ],
  "text": "Comprehensive narrative explaining the end-to-end flow, citing specific files and functions from each repo."
}
```

**Important**: Use the exact repo identifiers specified for this task. The oracle expects `repo` values of `sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go` (client layer), `kubernetes/kubernetes` (API server layer), and `etcd-io/etcd` (storage layer). The `repo` field must match these exactly.
**Note**: Tool output may return repo names with a `github.com/` prefix (e.g., `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go`). Strip this prefix in your answer — use `sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go`, NOT `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go`.

The `chain` should contain at least 3 steps representing the 3 layers described above.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **Flow coverage**: Does the chain include key steps from all 3 layers (client → server → storage)?
- **Technical accuracy**: Are the cited file paths and function names correct?
- **Provenance**: Does your narrative reference all three repositories?
- **Synthesis quality** (supplementary): Does the explanation connect the layers clearly?

    30→type Bucket interface {
    31→	// ID returns a unique identifier of a bucket.
    32→	// The id must NOT be persisted and can be used as lightweight identificator
    33→	// in the in-memory maps.

    40→	// overwrites on a bucket should only fetch with limit=1, but safeRangeBucket
    41→	// is known to never overwrite any key so range is safe.
    42→	IsSafeRangeBucket() bool
    43→}

87-usertool_resultRead
   149→func (t *batchTx) unsafePut(bucketType Bucket, key []byte, value []byte, seq bool) {
   150→	bucket := t.tx.Bucket(bucketType.Name())
   151→	if bucket == nil {
   152→		t.backend.lg.Fatal(
   153→			"failed to find a bucket",
   154→			zap.Stringer("bucket-name", bucketType),
   155→			zap.Stack("stack"),
   156→		)
   157→	}
   158→	if seq {
   159→		// it is useful to increase fill percent when the workloads are mostly append-only.
   160→		// this can delay the page split and reduce space usage.
   161→		bucket.FillPercent = 0.9
   162→	}
   163→	if err := bucket.Put(key, value); err != nil {
   164→		t.backend.lg.Fatal(
   165→			"failed to write to a bucket",
   166→			zap.Stringer("bucket-name", bucketType),
   167→			zap.Error(err),
   168→		)
   169→	}
   170→	t.pending++
   171→}
   172→
   173→// UnsafeRange must be called holding the lock on the tx.
   174→func (t *batchTx) UnsafeRange(bucketType Bucket, key, endKey []byte, limit int64) ([][]byte, [][]byte) {
   175→	bucket := t.tx.Bucket(bucketType.Name())
   176→	if bucket == nil {
   177→		t.backend.lg.Fatal(
   178→			"failed to find a bucket",
   179→			zap.Stringer("bucket-name", bucketType),
   180→			zap.Stack("stack"),
   181→		)
   182→	}
   183→	return unsafeRange(bucket.Cursor(), key, endKey, limit)
   184→}
   185→
   186→func unsafeRange(c *bolt.Cursor, key, endKey []byte, limit int64) (keys [][]byte, vs [][]byte) {
   187→	if limit <= 0 {
   188→		limit = math.MaxInt64
   189→	}
   190→	var isMatch func(b []byte) bool
   191→	if len(endKey) > 0 {
   192→		isMatch = func(b []byte) bool { return bytes.Compare(b, endKey) < 0 }
   193→	} else {
   194→		isMatch = func(b []byte) bool { return bytes.Equal(b, key) }
   195→		limit = 1
   196→	}
   197→
   198→	for ck, cv := c.Seek(key); ck != 
... (truncated)

   255→		trace = traceutil.New("put",
   256→			a.s.Logger(),
   257→			traceutil.Field{Key: "key", Value: string(p.Key)},
   258→			traceutil.Field{Key: "req_size", Value: p.Size()},
   259→		)
   260→	}

   265→				return nil, nil, lease.ErrLeaseNotFound
   266→			}
   267→		}

   269→		defer txn.End()
   270→	}

   275→			rr, err = txn.Range(context.TODO(), p.Key, nil, mvcc.RangeOptions{})
   276→		}, "get previous kv pair")
   277→
   278→		if err != nil {
   279→			return nil, nil, err
   280→		}
   281→	}
   282→	if p.IgnoreValue || p.IgnoreLease {
   283→		if rr == nil || len(rr.KVs) == 0 {
   284→			// ignore_{lease,value} flag expects previous key-value pair

   300→	resp.Header.Revision = txn.Put(p.Key, val, leaseID)
   301→	trace.AddField(traceutil.Field{Key: "response_revision", Value: resp.Header.Revision})
   302→	return resp, trace, nil
   303→}
   304→
   305→func (a *applierV3backend) DeleteRange(txn mvcc.TxnWrite, dr *pb.DeleteRangeRequest) (*pb.DeleteRangeResponse, error) {
   306→	resp := &pb.DeleteRangeResponse{}
   307→	resp.Header = &pb.ResponseHeader{}
   308→	end := mkGteRange(dr.RangeEnd)
   309→
   310→	if txn == nil {
   311→		txn = a.s.kv.Write(traceutil.TODO())
   312→		defer txn.End()
   313→	}
   314→
   315→	if dr.PrevKv {
   316→		rr, err := txn.Range(context.TODO(), dr.Key, end, mvcc.RangeOptions{})
   317→		if err != nil {
   318→			return nil, err
   319→		}
   320→		if rr != nil {
   321→			resp.PrevKvs = make([]*mvccpb.KeyValue, len(rr.KVs))
   322→			for i := range rr.KVs {
   323→				resp.PrevKvs[i] = &rr.KVs[i]
   324→			}
   325→		}
   326→	}

   241→// Commit commits a previous tx and begins a new writable one.
   242→func (t *batchTx) Commit() {
   243→	t.lock()
   244→	t.commit(false)
   245→	t.Unlock()
   246→}
   247→
   248→// CommitAndStop commits the previous tx and does not create a new one.
   249→func (t *batchTx) CommitAndStop() {
   250→	t.lock()
   251→	t.commit(true)
   252→	t.Unlock()
   253→}
   254→
   255→func (t *batchTx) safePending() int {
   256→	t.Mutex.Lock()
   257→	defer t.Mutex.Unlock()
   258→	return t.pending
   259→}
   260→
   261→func (t *batchTx) commit(stop bool) {
   262→	// commit the last tx
   263→	if t.tx != nil {
   264→		if t.pending == 0 && !stop {
   265→			return
   266→		}
   267→
   268→		start := time.Now()
   269→
   270→		// gofail: var beforeCommit struct{}
   271→		err := t.tx.Commit()
   272→		// gofail: var afterCommit struct{}
   273→
   274→		rebalanceSec.Observe(t.tx.Stats().RebalanceTime.Seconds())
   275→		spillSec.Observe(t.tx.Stats().SpillTime.Seconds())
   276→		writeSec.Observe(t.tx.Stats().WriteTime.Seconds())
   277→		commitSec.Observe(time.Since(start).Seconds())
   278→		atomic.AddInt64(&t.backend.commits, 1)
   279→
   280→		t.pending = 0

The `Create` method is implemented in the generic client:
```go
func (c *Client[T]) Create(ctx context.Context, obj T, opts metav1.CreateOptions) (T, error) {
	result := c.newObject()
	err := c.client.Post().
		UseProtobufAsDefaultIfPreferred(c.prefersProtobuf).
		NamespaceIfScoped(c.namespace, c.namespace != "").
		Resource(c.resource).
		VersionedParams(&opts, c.parameterCodec).
		Body(obj).
		Do(ctx).
		Into(result)
	return result, err
}
```

**Key Points:**
- Uses HTTP POST method (`c.client.Post()`)
- Constructs the REST request with namespace and resource path
- Serializes the Deployment object in the request body
- Executes the request with `Do(ctx)` and deserial

## Summary

I've traced the complete end-to-end flow of how a Kubernetes Deployment gets created through all three layers:

### **Client Layer** (sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go)
- **DeploymentInterface** in `kubernetes/typed/apps/v1/deployment.go` - defines the public Create method
- **Client[T].Create** in `gentype/type.go` - constructs and sends the HTTP POST request

### **API Server Layer** (kubernetes/kubernetes)
- **createHandler** in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/create.go` - receives the HTTP request
- **Store.Create** in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go` - validates and processes the Deployment
- **DeploymentStorage** in `pkg/registry/apps/deployment/storage/storage.go` - Deployment-specific REST handler

### **Storage Layer** (etcd-io/etcd)
- **applierV3backend.Put** in `server/etcdserver/apply.go` - etcd's Put handler
- **storeTxnWrite.put** in `server/mvcc/kvstore_txn.go` - MVCC transaction marshaling
- **batchTx.unsafePut** in `server/mvcc/backend/batch_tx.go` - low-level BoltDB write
- **batchTx.commit** in `server/mvcc/backend/batch_tx.go` - durability via disk flush

The answer includes a comprehensive narrative with a complete request flow diagram and explanations of key design principles like separation of concerns, generic architecture, transaction safety, and buffered writes.

Each layer has specific responsibilities in validating, processing, and persisting the Deployment object.\\n\\n## Layer 1: Client Library (sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go)\\n\\n### Entry Point: DeploymentInterface\\n\\nThe journey begins in the Go client library at `kubernetes/typed/apps/v1/deployment.go`, where the `DeploymentInterface` defines the public API. This is a generic storage handler used by all Kubernetes resources. The `Store.Create` method:\\n\\n1. Calls the underlying storage backend's `Create` method with a storage key and the serialized object\\n\\n### Deployment-Specific Configuration: DeploymentStorage\\n\\nThe API server's deployment storage in `pkg/registry/apps/deployment/storage/storage.go` registers the Deployment REST handler. The `DeploymentStorage` type contains the `REST` field, which embeds the generic `Store` with deployment-specific configuration:\\n\\n- **CreateStrategy**: Uses `deployment.Strategy` to define validation and preparation logic\\n- **Storage key pattern**: `deployments.apps` in etcd (scoped to namespace if applicable)\\n- **Subresources**: Also exposes `/status`, `/scale`, and `/rollback` endpoints\\n\\n## Layer 3: etcd Storage (etcd-io/etcd)\\n\\n### API Handler: applierV3backend.Put\\n\\nOnce the Kubernetes API server has validated the Deployment, it calls the storage backend's `Create` method, which ultimately results in a Put request to etcd. In `server/etcdserver/apply.go`, the `applierV3backend.Put` function:\\n\\n1. Validates lease information\\n2. Retrieves previous KV values if needed\\n3. Buffers the write in a transaction (not yet persisted to disk)\\n\\n### Durability: batchTx.commit\\n\\nFinally, the `batchTx.commit` function ensures durability:\\n\\n1.
